  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1f6d0979-07a1-4caa-a595-6d9279b9adb4'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18293074701129933818">A thought provoking checklist for dog lovers, who unfortunately, and with much sadness, can no longer take care of their dog. This book will assist those who want to prepare for their dog's future in an easy-to-use format that will guide them through the process of telling the "story" of their dog's life, for their pet's "Next Guardian." None of us can predict the future, </span>
  <span id="freeText18293074701129933818" style="display:none">A thought provoking checklist for dog lovers, who unfortunately, and with much sadness, can no longer take care of their dog. This book will assist those who want to prepare for their dog's future in an easy-to-use format that will guide them through the process of telling the "story" of their dog's life, for their pet's "Next Guardian." None of us can predict the future, but in the event situations arise such as death, health impairment, or left with no other choice but to give them up, this book will be there to assist your beloved pet with the transition from one home to another.</span>

<div id="review_658168658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/658168658" />
    <a title="Beem Weeks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14435475-beem-weeks"><img alt="Beem Weeks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598808013p2/14435475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/658168658?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beem Weeks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beem Weeks" href="/user/show/14435475-beem-weeks">Beem Weeks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer658168658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5132311296856134412">This isn't your typical book. It doesn't tell the reader a story the way a novel does. That being said, this book is really quite brilliant. Every dog owner needs to purchase this unique work.<br/><br/>Joe and Cathy Connolly have created the very voice of your K9 companion. As the title suggests, suppose you, a pet owner, die before your pooch? Or maybe you're injured and are no longer capable of caring for your dog. Would you be comfortable with your four-legged companion going to a new home that knows a</span>
  <span id="freeText5132311296856134412" style="display:none">This isn't your typical book. It doesn't tell the reader a story the way a novel does. That being said, this book is really quite brilliant. Every dog owner needs to purchase this unique work.<br /><br />Joe and Cathy Connolly have created the very voice of your K9 companion. As the title suggests, suppose you, a pet owner, die before your pooch? Or maybe you're injured and are no longer capable of caring for your dog. Would you be comfortable with your four-legged companion going to a new home that knows absolutely nothing about your friend? Those of us who have or have had dogs know they often become part of our families. They are almost like our children. If something happens to the owner, well, that pet could go to a new home that, while a good home, may not be a pleasant experience for your friend. <br /><br />Joe and Cathy have put together a book, sort of similar to a medical file, that documents your dog's favorite food, sleeping habits, medical issues; it informs the new owner all about the things that frighten the pooch, that make him/her feel comfortable, or those bad habits Fido may possess and just how to deal with them. The book covers many aspects of a dog's life. It is, as I mentioned above, the very voice of your pet. <br /><br />We plan ahead for our loved ones(children, spouse), in the event of our demise or incapacitation; but what do we do for our pets? They can't speak for themselves. The change in home and life circumstances are often scary and confusing for the dog. This book, to be completed by the pet's owner, is meant to make those unfortunate transitions easier for the dog. I suppose this might even be a book for cats as well, though it specifically deals with dogs. <br /><br />If you have a pet you care about, give yourself peace of mind by assuring an easier move--should the unfortunate occur. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5132311296856134412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_480097986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/480097986" />
    <a title="Ruth Hill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2299424-ruth-hill"><img alt="Ruth Hill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304129027p2/2299424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/480097986?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruth Hill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruth Hill" href="/user/show/2299424-ruth-hill">Ruth Hill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2299424-ruth-hill?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer480097986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8277085097018733455">When I first heard about this book, I was initially intrigued. I love the fact that the book addresses something we don't often think about. We make provisions for our children, but in many cases, dogs have become as much a part of the family as our kids (and they may even take the place of children we never had). How do you go about making sure your animals are provided for if you happen to meet an unexpected, sudden death? You certainly don't want them wandering around without any care, and I </span>
  <span id="freeText8277085097018733455" style="display:none">When I first heard about this book, I was initially intrigued. I love the fact that the book addresses something we don't often think about. We make provisions for our children, but in many cases, dogs have become as much a part of the family as our kids (and they may even take the place of children we never had). How do you go about making sure your animals are provided for if you happen to meet an unexpected, sudden death? You certainly don't want them wandering around without any care, and I bet you don't want them to go to a shelter and potentially be put down. These are things you must think about, but where do you begin?<br /><br />This is a practical book with a lot of help for owners to see that their dogs are cared for. They even talk about providing care for your animals in the event that you are physically or mentally unable to care for them. It's not always about death. The possibilities are endless. <br /><br />I am a dog lover, and although we have but one dog, we have 13 cats and four goats. It makes me think that the principles of this book will spill over into preparing to have your other animals taken care of in the event of your untimely demise. This book definitely fills a niche that I have not seen elsewhere, and hopefully it will resonate with readers.<br /><br />I was thoroughly amazed at how comprehensive this guide was. I saw that it would work for my daughter's cat or any of the dear animals we have in our lives. (We also have four goats.) I could even see some of these charts being used to long-term care. I was horrified to discover the other day that some people actually have their animal euthanized following their death. I can't imagine doing that (or those you leave behind doing that to your animal). This book should offer a simple but thorough guide to ensuring your animal gets the best care when you are no longer there to provide it.<br /><br />I was sent a copy of this book in exchange for my honest review. I was not financially compensated, and all opinions are 100 percent mine.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8277085097018733455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer477185143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer919881377834552936">If I Should Die Before My Dog --- is that important of a resource that every dog owner should have this book filled out and in a safe place.<br/><br/>If you have a dog you should have a copy of this book. It is so important to plan for your dog(s) future if you are no longer able to care for them. It helps ease the horrible transition for your dog if something happens to you so that your dog’s basic routine is followed as much as possible. It helps you to remember to write down the small details and the b</span>
  <span id="freeText919881377834552936" style="display:none">If I Should Die Before My Dog --- is that important of a resource that every dog owner should have this book filled out and in a safe place.<br /><br />If you have a dog you should have a copy of this book. It is so important to plan for your dog(s) future if you are no longer able to care for them. It helps ease the horrible transition for your dog if something happens to you so that your dog’s basic routine is followed as much as possible. It helps you to remember to write down the small details and the big ones about your dog's life. <br /><br />Even if you put your dog in your WILL it could take weeks or months for it to be read and any legal matters handled during which time your dog is in limbo if no one knows what was supposed to be done. This book is the key to making sure that your wishes are carried out and your dog remains safe and cared for. </span>

<div id="review_466041866" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466041866" />
    <a title="Sharon Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5761253-sharon-martin"><img alt="Sharon Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483445218p2/5761253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466041866?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Martin" href="/user/show/5761253-sharon-martin">Sharon Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5761253-sharon-martin?shelf=beck-valley-book-tours">beck-valley-book-tours</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466041866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1523845494151612948">Out of all the books I have reviewed this must be the most important and special book of them all. Almost all dog owners, including myself, never want to think about the unimaginable heartbreaking and devastating event of not being there to love and care for their dog. It will certainly make you think, especially after reading Mandy's and Bob's sudden change of circumstances. With no explanation or way to communicate 'why', the only thing we can do is to ensure that, in our own words, they will </span>
  <span id="freeText1523845494151612948" style="display:none">Out of all the books I have reviewed this must be the most important and special book of them all. Almost all dog owners, including myself, never want to think about the unimaginable heartbreaking and devastating event of not being there to love and care for their dog. It will certainly make you think, especially after reading Mandy's and Bob's sudden change of circumstances. With no explanation or way to communicate 'why', the only thing we can do is to ensure that, in our own words, they will be loved and cared for to the highest possible degree by giving as much information to the next carer as possible.<br /><br />The book may be emotional to look through and complete, it was for me especially when one of my dogs was laid next to me as I was reading it, but it will also make you smile with some of the memories that you fill in. Two parts to the book certainly made me smile - Words I Know for example Ice-Cream and My Bad Habits and How To Prevent Them, especially as it shows a Labrador with a trainer in it's mouth just like my Border Terrier. <br /><br />If allowed, my Border Terrier, can be extremely naughty and temperamental so it is vital that any new owner knows how to tackle his behaviour and can show him who the boss is from the start. For my Border Collie she is a very shy and nervous lady and I need to put across how she reacts and tries to control this herself.<br /><br />There are some absolutely beautiful illustrations in the book, my particular favourite is a picture of an angel being shown the dogs treasured life story by the owner as the dog sits next to them. Words of wisdom and information are also part of the book as you read through each part. There is also a beautiful worded note from the dog to it's new owner towards the back along with extra pages titled 'Special Things From My Human'.<br /><br />As well as vital information such as medical history, insurance cover, personality, food and snack preferences, the book also covers those special intimate details about their characteristics, how they like to be groomed, do they like to be held, habits, do they like the phone and so on.<br /><br />A unique, well thought out, beautifully illustrated treasured book for all dog lovers which can also be kept as a loving memory of your dogs life, if you never have to use it's main purpose. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1523845494151612948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13946716045037942534" style="display:none">As a mom I joyously recall filling in the empty spaces of a baby book for my son for the first few years of his life. A photo, a lock of hair, a list of his favorite toddler toys... <br /><br />Joe Connolly and Cathy Connolly must know the joy these memory books bring to baby's family members' hearts; for between the covers of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16125481._If_I_Should_Die_Before_My_Dog___" title="&quot;If I Should Die Before My Dog__&quot; by Joe and Cathy Connolly" rel="nofollow noopener">"If I Should Die Before My Dog__"</a> are similar pages with spaces for similar notations of your beloved dog.<br /><br />Make no mistake...<br /><br />"If I Should Die Before My Dog --" is much more than a memory book. It is the foundation for preparing a future for your precious pooch without you in it.<br /><br />Each page of the book is a step on the pathway to finding a new home for your dog should you no longer be able to provide that home. You will designate a special person to become the carer of your dog in your absence. You will share with this person every important piece of information about your dog and the seemingly not-so-important details too.<br /><br />These will be the needful things your dog's new owner will embrace in order to make your beloved dog feel at home.<br /><br />Sure, your dog will miss you, will never forget you, but the memories will be sweet when all of his favorite things are there to remind him of you.<br /><br />Do yourself and your dog a favor and grab a copy of "If I Should Die Before My Dog --". Grab a book for a friend or two, too. It would be a blessed gift for all of you no matter what the future holds.</span>

<div id="review_520625300" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/520625300" />
    <a title="Leslie Olyott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13678944-leslie-olyott"><img alt="Leslie Olyott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350390640p2/13678944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/520625300?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie Olyott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie Olyott" href="/user/show/13678944-leslie-olyott">Leslie Olyott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer520625300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1283437174381232480">Most of us have experienced the pain of losing a beloved pet. But I wonder how many have given much thought to how our pet would feel were they to suddenly lose us? What would happen to them? Who would feed them? Who would take them for walks, understand their needs and know that they prefer the yellow duck to the green dragon to sleep with at night?<br/><br/>Authors Joe and Cathy Connolly have thought about all those questions and wrote "If I Should Die Before My Dog -" to get you thinking about it, too.</span>
  <span id="freeText1283437174381232480" style="display:none">Most of us have experienced the pain of losing a beloved pet. But I wonder how many have given much thought to how our pet would feel were they to suddenly lose us? What would happen to them? Who would feed them? Who would take them for walks, understand their needs and know that they prefer the yellow duck to the green dragon to sleep with at night?<br /><br />Authors Joe and Cathy Connolly have thought about all those questions and wrote "If I Should Die Before My Dog -" to get you thinking about it, too.<br /><br />"If I Should Die Before My Dog -" is a workbook that helps guide pet parents through the process of preparing a new life for your dog in the event you are no longer able to take care of them. Told from the perspective of your dog, the book addresses the dog's health and heritage, likes and fears and tricks and treats.<br /><br />And it does so in great detail.<br /><br />Joe and Cathy don't just ask the requisite questions like "Who's my vet?" and "How much do I eat?" They ask if the dog likes to go to the vet or is afraid. They ask about the kind of food the dog eats and if they're allowed table scraps and what their favorite snack is. They ask what kinds of medications the dog takes and give plenty of room to elaborate on past or current medical concerns.<br /><br />I hope everyone who has a dog they love in their life will read this book and think about their answers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1283437174381232480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_632556140" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/632556140" />
    <a title="Jody Zimmerman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13304497-jody-zimmerman"><img alt="Jody Zimmerman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414081207p2/13304497.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/632556140?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody Zimmerman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody Zimmerman" href="/user/show/13304497-jody-zimmerman">Jody Zimmerman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer632556140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7455149454606756155">Joe and Cathy Connolly's book, If I Should Die Before My Dog--, is a comprehensive care plan for dog owners who are approaching the end of their life or otherwise will be unable to care for their beloved pet in the near future. The book provides fill in the blank forms concerning almost everything you could think of affecting a dog's well being from the types of food and medicines he needs to his idiosyncrasies to small pleasures he enjoys.<br/><br/>As a volunteer for various animal rescues and humane org</span>
  <span id="freeText7455149454606756155" style="display:none">Joe and Cathy Connolly's book, If I Should Die Before My Dog--, is a comprehensive care plan for dog owners who are approaching the end of their life or otherwise will be unable to care for their beloved pet in the near future. The book provides fill in the blank forms concerning almost everything you could think of affecting a dog's well being from the types of food and medicines he needs to his idiosyncrasies to small pleasures he enjoys.<br /><br />As a volunteer for various animal rescues and humane organizations over the years, I have seen far too many dogs and cats sent to shelters with absolutely no information other than their name and sometimes age, after an owner's death or inability, for whatever reason, to care for their pet. This book will certainly enable interim caregivers to provide a higher quality of life for a pet who is often depressed and grieving and create a higher chance of placing the pet in a suitable permanent home.<br /><br />The book is well-written, easy to read, and well organized with beautiful illustrations by Rod Lawrence. It is a quick read, but puts our focus where it should be for creatures that give us so much love. I estimate owners could spend several hours completing the care plan for each pet. I know I will. This book could also be used for any species of pet. If you love your dog and want to ensure the continuance of a good quality life in the event of your death or untimely demise, please buy this book. This book will also make a great gift for all your friends with pets. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7455149454606756155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_527580113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527580113" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14369200-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352336117p2/14369200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527580113?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/14369200-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527580113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7821189139552949023">Three years ago, I adopted a beautiful Collie/Border Collie mix from a rescue group who saved her from a very high-kill southern shelter. This gorgeous, well trained 8 year old dog's owner had passed away. He thought his family was going to take care of her, but instead they turned around and dumped her in a shelter with an over 80% kill rate.<br/><br/>Cheyenne was one of the lucky ones. An amazing rescue group saved her on "kill day" right before she was scheduled to be euthanized. And she found the perf</span>
  <span id="freeText7821189139552949023" style="display:none">Three years ago, I adopted a beautiful Collie/Border Collie mix from a rescue group who saved her from a very high-kill southern shelter. This gorgeous, well trained 8 year old dog's owner had passed away. He thought his family was going to take care of her, but instead they turned around and dumped her in a shelter with an over 80% kill rate.<br /><br />Cheyenne was one of the lucky ones. An amazing rescue group saved her on "kill day" right before she was scheduled to be euthanized. And she found the perfect home with me- she's spoiled, she's healthy, she's loved. But so many dogs aren't that lucky.<br /><br />If you were to die tomorrow, do you know what would happen to your dogs? Do you know who would take them in- and do you have backups in case that situation falls through? Thankfully, many people do have some sort of plan in place- even going so far is to include provisions for pets in their wills. But does the person you've entrusted your pet to know everything they will need to know to provide the best care they can for your dog?<br /><br />Cheyenne is happy with us, but there was definitely some trial and error, and an "instruction manual" certainly would have been helpful. "If I Should Die Before My Dog" is just that- an instruction manual for those who have- whatever the circumstances- overtaken the care of your dog. It doesn't take long to read or to fill out, but provides a wealth of information for your dog's new caretaker.<br /><br />I know where my dogs would go if I were to die tomorrow- and I know who my backups would be if my first choices were to fall through. And all of those people know what my wishes are. They know my dogs- but no matter how often they visit, they won't know the quirks and intricacies that every owner comes to know about their dogs daily lives. "If I Should Die Before My Dog" will help provide a smoother transition. My sister would be able to look and find that Cheyenne is terrified of thunderstorms- but that it is easily managed with her Thundershirt, some Comfort Zone sprayed on a bandanna around her neck, and some soothing words. Or that Shiloh (my younger Sheltie) is very allergic to and cannot receive the leptospirosis vaccine. Or that both dogs know a long list of tricks, but all the commands and hand signals have been written down on pg86. And that they can spell- forwards AND backwards, so you'll need to come up with special code words for things like "walk" and "out" and "agility" or you'll have very eager collies herding you toward the back door. And maybe most importantly, if you give them a scratch on the butt or a taste of your spaghetti sauce, they will be your best friend for life.<br /><br />My dogs are my children, my best friends, and my entire life. They are unique individuals who have likes, dislikes, fears, favorites, health concerns, and, overall, histories. As a pet parent, I know each of these important aspects of my dogs's lives, and it is my job to pass along this information to those who I've entrusted in caring for them should I become unable. This book gives me some peace of mind knowing that my pet's next caretaker will have a greater understanding of who my dogs are and what they need. "If I Should Die Before My Dog" is an absolute must have for all dog owners.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7821189139552949023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_525053054" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/525053054" />
    <a title="GIZMO" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10696161-gizmo"><img alt="GIZMO" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359898182p2/10696161.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/525053054?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GIZMO" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GIZMO" href="/user/show/10696161-gizmo">GIZMO</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer525053054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12560291064856944466">Shortly after my last birthday I decided it was time for me to do some personal estate planning. There was no immediacy to this decision, but I’d entered the decade of life where these thoughts come to mind. <br/><br/>I knew that disposing of my “stuff” would be no problem. The big question is what would happen to my best friend. I’m lucky in that I’m good friends with a couple with whom I exchange pet-sitting favors. When they need, Gizmo & I stay at their place and watch their pack, and whenever I have </span>
  <span id="freeText12560291064856944466" style="display:none">Shortly after my last birthday I decided it was time for me to do some personal estate planning. There was no immediacy to this decision, but I’d entered the decade of life where these thoughts come to mind. <br /><br />I knew that disposing of my “stuff” would be no problem. The big question is what would happen to my best friend. I’m lucky in that I’m good friends with a couple with whom I exchange pet-sitting favors. When they need, Gizmo &amp; I stay at their place and watch their pack, and whenever I have to leave, Gizmo goes to stay with them. He’s very comfortable in their home and they love him. I approached each of them separately and asked if they would be willing to adopt Gizmo if anything ever happened to me. I felt it was important that they both were willing, and happily they were. Problem settled…or so I thought.<br /><br />It was a stroke of luck that I was invited to review “If I Should die Before My Dog —“, by Joe and Cathy Connolly. Although my friends know Gizmo, this book made me realize that they didn’t really “know” him.<br /><br /><br /><br />The format is that of a workbook or diary of your dog’s life. As I reviewed the questions I realized that there was so much about Gizmo that no one but me really knew. Won’t it be wonderful to provide Gizmo’s next guardians with detailed information so that they can comfort him and ease his sadness and confusion when I’m no longer there for him. <br /><br />This is such a difficult subject for any of us to think about, but the Connolly’s guide you through it gently, in a positive tone, and from your dog’s point of view. When completed, the reader will hear your dog telling his own story.<br /><br />Every aspect of your dog’s life is considered here, and in detail that wouldn’t have occurred to me. For example, would I have thought to include a list of Gizmo’s nicknames? Probably not. How about his microchip information? I would have missed that one too. When I got to the section on how Gizmo signaled he that he needed to go out I included a note that he’s used to having a bell hanging from the doorknob that he taps when it’s time…never would have remembered to add that without the Connolly’s prompting. There’s almost 30 key aspects of your dog’s life covered here, and if you take the time to fill in each section you will be presenting your dog’s next caretakers with a fully complete guide to his unique and loveable self.<br /><br />The last section of the book is called “What I’d Like to Relate”. This was probably the hardest for me to complete. It’s where you can write a letter to your dog, saying whatever you want. This was the only section that saddened me, realizing that I would not be the person to read this to Gizmo.<br /><br />I’ll be leaving this completed book with my attorney, to provide to Gizmo’s new home if and when necessary.<br /><br />I recommend that everyone who loves their pets and cares about what happens to them get this book and take the time to complete it in detail. Not to be morbid, but you don’t have to be “of a certain age” to make use of this. Tragic accidents can happen, and where your dog is concerned, being fully prepared is always best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12560291064856944466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474781727?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/4619750-ashley">Ashley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13669080014146939503">This has been one of my favorite assignments with MVM Book Reviews :) It really really is a book that is now close to my heart. It is also one of the hardest for me to write.<br/><br/>We (my fiance and I) have two Mal-shi dogs. One of my Mal-shi pups was hit by a car on February 29th, 2012. Before this event I had no clue that dogs and pets actually grieve. We were devastated of course but our little girl was beyond devastated. She stopped eating, would constantly whine and cry especially after she would </span>
  <span id="freeText13669080014146939503" style="display:none">This has been one of my favorite assignments with MVM Book Reviews :) It really really is a book that is now close to my heart. It is also one of the hardest for me to write.<br /><br />We (my fiance and I) have two Mal-shi dogs. One of my Mal-shi pups was hit by a car on February 29th, 2012. Before this event I had no clue that dogs and pets actually grieve. We were devastated of course but our little girl was beyond devastated. She stopped eating, would constantly whine and cry especially after she would look around for him and not find him, they had never been apart her whole life, he was 3 she was not even a year old. I could almost hear her pleas and screams as I was forced to watch this seemingly endless cycle. She lost her best friend, her partner in crime, her love. Now if we were to leave our pets unexpectedly I can not even imagine how they would handle it. I am lucky enough to have a mother who would take them in a heartbeat and knows everything there is to know about them and their quirks (we have since bought Lilly a friend -actually less than a week later and she perked up within a day. They are the best of friends now) but if my mom was not around I would need this book more than anything else in my possession. <br /><br />When there is a death people are not always prepared for the care of their pets and other people can easily over look a dog or cat especially if they do not have pets themselves. This book is perfect for making sure the furry friends you love most are taken care of if you should die before your pet. From the schedules to vets to groomers to treats and food, you need to leave directions for your babies. I plan on keeping this book in my fire-proof box with our wills and all of our other important documents. <br /><br />My favorite sections of the books are these:<br /><br />1. Riding in the Car: My girls get car sick and we have to give them what we call "the juice" to keep them calm or they will get car sick everywhere (we found this out about 40 minutes into our first 9 hour car trip with them. Fun stuff right?!)<br /><br />2. Grooming: My babies love their groomer Andrew at Little Critters. He understands them and knows exactly what we like them to look like. They are family there at Little Critters and if I wasn't around I would want them to still have their normalcy as much as possible. <br /><br />and finally<br /><br />3. Nicknames: My babies have nicknames that they know. Their names are Lilly Pad and Olivia Grace but they answer to Lilly, Pad, Livie, Smushface, snotter, baby girl, and just simply girls. These are little touches that someone other than myself and my fiance may or may not know and they need that continuity. <br /><br />I implore you to go and get this book and fill it out so that your babies are not left without directions :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13669080014146939503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_529647024" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/529647024" />
    <a title="Nikki Epple" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17254326-nikki-epple"><img alt="Nikki Epple" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554980003p2/17254326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/529647024?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki Epple" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki Epple" href="/user/show/17254326-nikki-epple">Nikki Epple</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer529647024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13891160543410574670">The preface of the book shares the stories of two dogs and what happened to them after their owners passed. My parents both passed at early ages, my mother was 52 and my father was 62. Although, Dad had a diagnosis a few years before he passed, he still didn't prepare everything the way he should have and it was lucky that I was an adult because goodness knows what would have happened to me if I was a minor. That's how I feel about my little dogs Sandwich and Toot-Toot. They will always be littl</span>
  <span id="freeText13891160543410574670" style="display:none">The preface of the book shares the stories of two dogs and what happened to them after their owners passed. My parents both passed at early ages, my mother was 52 and my father was 62. Although, Dad had a diagnosis a few years before he passed, he still didn't prepare everything the way he should have and it was lucky that I was an adult because goodness knows what would have happened to me if I was a minor. That's how I feel about my little dogs Sandwich and Toot-Toot. They will always be little minors and while they have two mostly healthy parents, I'm so glad this book came to me serendipitously. I've wondered a couple times what would happen to my fur children if both Brad, my husband and I passed unexpectedly, but now I am so happy I have this book to serve as a will for what to do with Sandwich and Toot-Toot should something happen to both of their parents.<br /><br />When thinking about who you're dog(s) will go to should something happen, it's a rarity to think of all of the things that are included in this book. Names, nicknames, vet information and medications seem like a given, but the inclusion of habits for "when nature calls", weather needs, grooming habits and sleeping arrangements is brilliant and a comfort to know that the person they go to will have all this information. My husband and I now know that Sandwich and Toot-Toot will have new parents who know they know how to sit, shake and lay down as well as Sandwiches super confident nature and Toot slightly wary nature. I would have never thought to leave a description of how my dogs like to ride in the car, but what a great thing to include! It's quite funny, by the way, that the picture of the dog in a car just happens to looks so much like how Sandwich rides.<br /><br />This book gives a voice to my dogs in the event of mine and my husbands passing. It is brilliantly thought out to include everything a new owner would need to know especially since our youngest has a lot more fears than our oldest. She's the one I worry won't take us being gone so easily. Sandwich might miss us for a couple days, but as long as he's in a place where he gets attention, he will be fine. I think every dog owner younger or older needs this book. It's just like a will for your human children. You hope you won't need it, but in the event you do, it is so great that you've taken the time to make sure your fur kids are cared for. The illustrations by Rod Lawrence compliment this book so well. Well done Joe and Kathy Connolly for creating a book that every dog owner should have!<br /><br />I received a complimentary copy of this book from the author in exchange for an honest review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13891160543410574670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_517342143" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/517342143" />
    <a title="K-koira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16816017-k-koira"><img alt="K-koira" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/517342143?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K-koira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K-koira" href="/user/show/16816017-k-koira">K-koira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer517342143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12364273173947137712">It is something none of us really want to think about. Or simply don't think we have to think about. Our pets have such short lives compared to our own, that it is easy to not think about what will happen to them if something happens to us. But really, we should.<br/><br/>That is what "If I Should Die Before My Dog --" is all about. This book guides us, step by step, over what we really need to think about and plan for our pets in case the worst happens to us. It is perhaps better called a manual, even. I</span>
  <span id="freeText12364273173947137712" style="display:none">It is something none of us really want to think about. Or simply don't think we have to think about. Our pets have such short lives compared to our own, that it is easy to not think about what will happen to them if something happens to us. But really, we should.<br /><br />That is what "If I Should Die Before My Dog --" is all about. This book guides us, step by step, over what we really need to think about and plan for our pets in case the worst happens to us. It is perhaps better called a manual, even. It tastefully and carefully guides you through all of the things you should think about for caring for your pet after your death, providing blanks in the book for you to fill out. <br /><br />Not only are there the basics, like who is going to take your dog (do you know the answer to even this most basic question?), but the more in depth questions as well. It gives you a chance to really share everything about your pet, from the daily routine to allergies to the food they like the best. What kind of play do they enjoy? Are they afraid of men wearing sunglasses? All of those little quirks can be written down, all in this one place. <br /><br />You may know the answer to all of these questions already. But even if you have it laid out in your will who will take your dog, there is no comparison to having something like this book, filled out and ready, to hand off to the new owner of your dog. Being able to give them this reference of your dog's whole life could make a huge difference to how easily your beloved family member settles in to their new life. I would say this is a must have for any dog owner. Hopefully, you will never have to pass it on. Hopefully, your dog will live out a long and happy life in your household. In which case this book would be a wonderful reminder of all of the little things you did together and what made your relationship so unique and important to you.<br /><br />I also think this book would be a wonderful thing to send along to a new home of a foster dog. Imagine being able to send off that long term foster dog with a manual to all of the likes, dislikes, routines, and the tiny little details of their lives with you. For a dog who has already had upheaval and potentially many home changes, something like this could help keep some consistency and stability in their already chaotic lives. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12364273173947137712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_468675816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468675816" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7974364-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330484126p2/7974364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468675816?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/7974364-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468675816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4060078653972897734">A Dog Lovers lasting guide.......An beautifully illustrated interactive book that one fills in all of the information about their dogs life in the event they can no longer care for them to help ensure your pets are taken care of.<br/>A thought provoking check list for dog lovers, who unfortunately and with much sadness can no longer take care of their dog. <br/><br/><br/>This book will assist those who want to prepare for their dogs future in an easy to use format that will guide them through the process of telling</span>
  <span id="freeText4060078653972897734" style="display:none">A Dog Lovers lasting guide.......An beautifully illustrated interactive book that one fills in all of the information about their dogs life in the event they can no longer care for them to help ensure your pets are taken care of.<br />A thought provoking check list for dog lovers, who unfortunately and with much sadness can no longer take care of their dog. <br /><br /><br />This book will assist those who want to prepare for their dogs future in an easy to use format that will guide them through the process of telling the "story" of their dogs life, for their pets "Next Guardian". <br /><br /><br />None of us can predict the future, but in the event situations arise such as death, health impairment or left with no other choice but to give them up, this book will be there to assist your beloved pet with the transition from one home to another.<br />If you are like me and have a fur baby, have you really given any thought about what would happen to them when you are gone? Allie, Tutu and Winnie (may she rest in peace) are a big part of our lives, but I never really gave any thought to providing for them after I am gone. But in this unique book entitled, "If I Should Die Before My Dog--" written by Joe and Cathy Connolly, dog owners are given step by step guidelines on how to make sure your fur baby is taken care of. It is like a baby book for dogs. I read the book but decided that it would be an awesome opportunity for Gracie to put her future vet skills to use. I let her fill out the forms in the book. Yes folks this book comes with forms to fill out almost like a how to guidebook on your dog. Now remember Gracie is 10 going on 40 but she loved this book. She felt secure knowing that the person who gets her "little sister" would know everything there is to know about her.<br /><br />If you are looking for a unique present this holiday season for a dog lover then this is the one for you. But just because the title has the word dog in it does not mean that you can not adapt it to your own pet. Yes it is that easy to use folks. I loved this book. I now know that Allie and Tutu will be safely cared for when we have passed. Can you say the same about your fur babies?<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4060078653972897734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_524350379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/524350379" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3450803-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/524350379?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" rel="nofollow" href="/user/show/3450803-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer524350379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2659278733991820376">If I Should I die before my Dog, by Joe and Cathy Connolly is a well thought out guide for any dog owner to ensure your furbaby's care when you can no longer do it yourself.<br/><br/>We have two dogs, Baby and Spot, I honestly never thought about the "what if" I cannot take care of them. With this book there's isn't anything read but full of pages you must fill out about your dog. Though titled "If I should die before my dog" I think this is a great all around book to have on hand in case anything happens</span>
  <span id="freeText2659278733991820376" style="display:none">If I Should I die before my Dog, by Joe and Cathy Connolly is a well thought out guide for any dog owner to ensure your furbaby's care when you can no longer do it yourself.<br /><br />We have two dogs, Baby and Spot, I honestly never thought about the "what if" I cannot take care of them. With this book there's isn't anything read but full of pages you must fill out about your dog. Though titled "If I should die before my dog" I think this is a great all around book to have on hand in case anything happens. You become, ill, or are unable to afford care for your pet, having this book filled out all about your dog can ensure whoever can and does take care of your pet, will have a great start in getting to know them.<br /><br />Baby &amp; Spot I know they look all grumpy, they don't smile well for photo's!<br /><br />This book covers everything someone would need to know about your pet if something were to happen to you. It covers medical history, insurance and all the in between about your dog's life. Is your pet friendly to strangers? Does he have a routine silly ways he likes to do things? The book covers it all and I found it very informative. If I were to ever take on a pet from someone this would be the perfect guide to get along with them. You won't have to wonder if the dog likes kids, or has a thing about a certain toy, noise or a fear or storms or worse get's sick on car rides! Our two dogs get car sick, a trick that helps them cope? Ice cubes during the ride! One of our dogs was older when we got him, I wish I had known things about him when we got him from his keeper. His fear of people walking up too fast on him, his fear of dog doors, his dislike of certain foods. These are things you should put in the book , tell your dog's life story to ensure his well being after you cannot care for him anymore.<br /><br />This is an essential book for all dog lovers, I highly recommend it for anyone with a dog.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2659278733991820376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_473031564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473031564" />
    <a title="Liz Terek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6022140-liz-terek"><img alt="Liz Terek" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473031564?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Terek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Terek" href="/user/show/6022140-liz-terek">Liz Terek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473031564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6936996403983128722">Joe & Cathy Connolly have created an interactive checklist with gorgeous illustrations to ease after death fears for dog owners. As many folks see their pets as extensions of their families, it makes sense to include care for them as well. <br/>	Having lost my father last year on Christmas Day, I’ve witnessed firsthand the grief a pet faces. Honestly, I had no idea an animal grieved the way that Dad’s dog did. Had my children & I not been there to help him cope, I wonder how the Chihuahua would have </span>
  <span id="freeText6936996403983128722" style="display:none">Joe &amp; Cathy Connolly have created an interactive checklist with gorgeous illustrations to ease after death fears for dog owners. As many folks see their pets as extensions of their families, it makes sense to include care for them as well. <br />	Having lost my father last year on Christmas Day, I’ve witnessed firsthand the grief a pet faces. Honestly, I had no idea an animal grieved the way that Dad’s dog did. Had my children &amp; I not been there to help him cope, I wonder how the Chihuahua would have fared. From scheduling to food preferences, there is certainly a lot to consider. <br />	From a personal standpoint, I was impressed with the section in the book about Commands. Tone of voice is very important. Caregivers know what to say, how to say it &amp; when. Strangers would not know these things. What a great thought to include! Special needs dogs who communicate with non-verbal clues would absolutely need a list made about them. If you have a loved one with a special needs pet, this is a must have for your book shelf.<br />	Another section that made me smile was the one about things that scare a dog. Just as children have different fears, animals do too. Including a list of the dog’s fears is a beautiful idea. What a difference this would make to future caregivers! <br />	When one begins to prepare for their death, there is comfort in knowing all is taken care of in their life. Those who are terminally ill have enough to think on without fretting over the needs of others even if it is for a pet’s care. Joe &amp; Cathy have provided a priceless service to these folks. People without pets may not grasp the magnitude of love one has for a dog. But, Joe &amp; Cathy do &amp; as a result, ‘If I Should Die Before My Dog-‘has provided comfort &amp; security for others. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6936996403983128722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467763608" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467763608?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Belinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Belinda" href="/user/show/7221421-belinda">Belinda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467763608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17218887236527571718">I have had a lot of health issues this year (including 6 surgeries with 2 of them requiring lengthy hospital stays). Hubby would stop home for a couple of hours, just long enough to basically let Triton (my 10 year old black lab/german shepard) out to potty and fill up his food and water dishes and then he would return to the hospital. During this time, one of my greatest concerns where that Triton was being neglected. Was he scared? Was he wondering where mommy (and daddy) where? One morning, b</span>
  <span id="freeText17218887236527571718" style="display:none">I have had a lot of health issues this year (including 6 surgeries with 2 of them requiring lengthy hospital stays). Hubby would stop home for a couple of hours, just long enough to basically let Triton (my 10 year old black lab/german shepard) out to potty and fill up his food and water dishes and then he would return to the hospital. During this time, one of my greatest concerns where that Triton was being neglected. Was he scared? Was he wondering where mommy (and daddy) where? One morning, before hubby came back to the hospital, he took several pictures of Triton, and it is very clear that he is looking for me (the first one shows him looking up the street, the second shows him looking at hubby, and the last shows him looking down the street). This also got me to thinking what would happen to him if something happened to myself or to hubby? Would anyone step up and take care of him? <br /><br />I wish I would have read <em>"If I Should Die Before My Dog--"</em> before all this stuff happened, it would have given me more peace of mind. This book provides a place to write all the important information about our beloved pets (nicknames, favorite types of foods, vet information, etc) that will make it easier for some one else to step up and take over care for them. We make plans for who will take care of our children, and who gets all our stuff if anything (God forbid) happens to us. Why not put the same care and thought in to who would take care of our pets?<br /><br />This is a definite must have for all pet parents and should be kept up-to-date and with all the other "important" papers.<br /><br />I received a copy for review purposes. However, all opinions are strictly my own</span>
  <a data-text-id="17218887236527571718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_472932953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472932953" />
    <a title="Nicki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7413288-nicki"><img alt="Nicki" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/472932953?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicki" href="/user/show/7413288-nicki">Nicki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer472932953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer393399032776105579">No one really wants to think about the time when we may not be able to care for our loved ones, including our pets. This book helps pet owners to provide another person with all the information needed to help make any transition smoother for their furry loved one. A few years ago my mother and stepfather took in a dog after its owner had passed away suddenly. The owner was a good friend of my stepfather's, but even so he really knew nothing about the dog. A book like this would have been a treas</span>
  <span id="freeText393399032776105579" style="display:none">No one really wants to think about the time when we may not be able to care for our loved ones, including our pets. This book helps pet owners to provide another person with all the information needed to help make any transition smoother for their furry loved one. A few years ago my mother and stepfather took in a dog after its owner had passed away suddenly. The owner was a good friend of my stepfather's, but even so he really knew nothing about the dog. A book like this would have been a treasure as they tried to help Christy (the dog) adjust to her new life. <br /><br />The book may be a bit emotional to complete. There may be tears over the thought of no longer being able to be with or care for your dog, but I honestly enjoyed going through the book. I loved thinking about things such as what my dog's favorite toy is, the funny little routines we have, and all the "bad" habits (more of thinking of how funny it would be to watch another person learn to deal with these habits haha) my dog has. The hardest part for me to think about was the last one, "Special Things from My Human," because it makes us think about what about ourselves we would want our pet to have. Special songs, routines, or even a note to them telling them how much we love them; I get tears in my eyes just thinking about it. <br /><br />Unfortunately we cannot predict the future, and it is best to be prepared while hoping for the best. The book could also be used for when you are on vacation or your pet is being cared for by another person for a short time, as it contains a lot of information. I would recommend this book for any dog owner. </span>
  <a data-text-id="393399032776105579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_691307351" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/691307351" />
    <a title="Laurie Hanan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/974024-laurie-hanan"><img alt="Laurie Hanan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318566416p2/974024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/691307351?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie Hanan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie Hanan" href="/user/show/974024-laurie-hanan">Laurie Hanan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer691307351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3275302732052076995">Anyone involved in dog rescue has heard this story all too often: a dog’s person has either passed away, or has been moved to a care facility. The dog has been dumped in a shelter by friends or relatives who are either unable, or can’t be bothered, to take the dog in. The dog is bewildered, frightened, and grieving. Often, the shelter or rescue group has no information about the dog. Everything is strange. Nobody understands, and he has no way to explain what he is feeling.<br/><br/>I’ve always dreaded th</span>
  <span id="freeText3275302732052076995" style="display:none">Anyone involved in dog rescue has heard this story all too often: a dog’s person has either passed away, or has been moved to a care facility. The dog has been dumped in a shelter by friends or relatives who are either unable, or can’t be bothered, to take the dog in. The dog is bewildered, frightened, and grieving. Often, the shelter or rescue group has no information about the dog. Everything is strange. Nobody understands, and he has no way to explain what he is feeling.<br /><br />I’ve always dreaded the day my beloved service dog will “cross the Rainbow Bridge”. Before I read this book, I had not wanted to consider a situation even worse than losing my closest companion. What if I should die before my dog? <br /><br />This book is a must for anyone who loves their dog. Get the hard copy, because the pages are designed to be filled out by you, to give your dog a voice if the unthinkable should happen. Keep it with your other important records. It will give your dog’s next caregiver pertinent information such as his name, his medical information, etc. But just as important, it includes pages on: crate training, my sleep habits, my potty habits, my groomer, my nicknames, tricks I know, words I understand, my favorite toys, things that scare me, and so much more. While this book can’t ease the grief your beloved companion will feel at losing you, these little bits of information will help his new caregiver transition him into a strange and unfamiliar household.<br /><br />I cried while reading this book. I cried while writing this review. So keep a box of tissues beside you, but this book is a MUST HAVE.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/470088700?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phaedra Seabolt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phaedra Seabolt" href="/user/show/6459325-phaedra-seabolt">Phaedra Seabolt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer470088700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12376645110632816025">This is a wonderful book. It's not really meant to be sat down and read, unless you are the one receiving the book already filled in. It is a journal for you to tell the story of your dog's life. In my situation, I filled it out for two dogs. It is really meant only for one, but there's enough space on the pages to write information for another dog if needed. The purpose of this journal is so that if something terrible were to happen to you, the person who would end up with your dog will be bett</span>
  <span id="freeText12376645110632816025" style="display:none">This is a wonderful book. It's not really meant to be sat down and read, unless you are the one receiving the book already filled in. It is a journal for you to tell the story of your dog's life. In my situation, I filled it out for two dogs. It is really meant only for one, but there's enough space on the pages to write information for another dog if needed. The purpose of this journal is so that if something terrible were to happen to you, the person who would end up with your dog will be better prepared to actually take care of him/her the way they are used to. You know the saying "You can't teach an old dog new tricks"? Well the truth to that saying lies in your dog developing his routine and not adjusting very well to people changing that routine. Your dog has a unique way to tell you when he needs to go outside, when he wants to go for a walk, when he isn't feeling good, etc. Your dog also is used to eating certain foods at certain times and only so much. If you were to leave your dog behind, how will the new owner know that your dog is say allergic to one brand of dog food and not another? How would they know that when your dog puts his head in your lap he is really trying to tell you that he needs to pee instead of wanting to be petted? These are all in this book. You are supposed to fill it out and put it in a safe place. I would say the best place would be to keep it with your will, where ever that may be. I would highly recommend this book for anyone with a dog they love dearly. I also hope to see something similar come available for cats.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12376645110632816025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1074867078096161745">I love my dogs, they are like my children and if something happened to me and my immediate family I feel happier if my dogs were taken care of in a way that I would like. If I Should Die Before My Dog is a brilliant book for writing down your wishes for your dog if something did happen to you.<br/><br/>It is basically an instruction manual for whoever takes care of your dog. It covers the basic things like name, age, d.o.b, nicknames that you might call your dog. For instance my dog is called Peppa but sh</span>
  <span id="freeText1074867078096161745" style="display:none">I love my dogs, they are like my children and if something happened to me and my immediate family I feel happier if my dogs were taken care of in a way that I would like. If I Should Die Before My Dog is a brilliant book for writing down your wishes for your dog if something did happen to you.<br /><br />It is basically an instruction manual for whoever takes care of your dog. It covers the basic things like name, age, d.o.b, nicknames that you might call your dog. For instance my dog is called Peppa but she is often called P or Peps. You can add whether you dog is a purebred or a cross-breed. Vet details including whether your dog likes to visit the vet or not. When it’s annual visit is, if it needs medication. If he/she has been spayed or neutered. Microchip number, what food it likes and generally care for the dog. If it goes to a grooming parlour for instance, my dogs are shih tzus and they go to the grooming parlour every 12 weeks for a haircut. You can add your grooming parlours details too.<br /><br />There is so much to add to this book that I know for sure nothing has been left out. I know my dogs will be looked after if I go before them and I feel a lot better knowing there is an instruction manual for them.<br /><br />If you have a dog then I would definitely recommend this book. Ok the chances are that you will outlive your dog but to be there is no harm in getting it and filling it in, just in case!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8821855093826708756">When you have a pet that you treat like part of the family, you can't even imagine what you would do if something happened to them.   <span id="freeText8821855093826708756" style="display:none">When you have a pet that you treat like part of the family, you can't even imagine what you would do if something happened to them. In most cases you will out live your pets and you will move on, it will be sad and you will mourn them, but you will understand what has happened. What should happen to your dog if you were to pass away first? Do you have plans in place? How detailed are those plans? Your dog will be lost, confused and unable to tell anyone anything. What a sad place to be in.<br />This just about broke my heart. I have a lot of planning for the future to do, I know that I am still relatively young and healthy but, anything could happen. I would hate to see my beloved dogs end up in an animal shelter. This book helps guide you in the right direction to plan for your dog's future without you, if by chance something were to happen. The thing I really love is it goes into so much detail because the dog can't tell you what frightens them, what commands they know, or if they like to be crated. <br />This is a must have for all dog owners!! Keep it in a safe place and let someone know you have it and most importantly...make sure it's filled out as fully as possible, for your pet's sake. When you're gone, they will be confused, depressed and the small things that someone else can know about what they are used to can help to make their days better.</span>
